1 AMEND House Committee Substitute for House Bill Nos. 2780 & 2668, Page 2, Section A,
2 Line 15, by inserting after all of said section and line the following:
3
4 "64.401. 1. Persons residing in an area adjacent to and within three miles of a
5 municipality that has formed and established a park system under sections 90.010 to 90.020 and
6 90.500 to 90.570 may petition to become part of the park system in the manner prescribed in this
7 subsection. The petition shall include a description of the territory to be embraced by the park
8 system, the provision for a tax to support the park system at the rate of tax which residents of the
9 municipality are required to pay to support the park system, and the signatures of five percent of
10 the qualified voters within the area outside the municipality as determined by the county clerk on
11 the basis of the number of votes cast in the area for governor in the last election held prior to
12 filing of the petition. The petition shall be filed with the governing body of the municipality and
13 the county clerk. The governing body of the municipality shall within thirty days of receipt of
14 the petition vote to approve or reject the request of the adjacent property owners to become part
15 of the municipal parks system at a regularly scheduled meeting of the governing body of the
16 municipality. The governing body of the municipality shall notify the county clerk of its action.
17 If the governing body of the municipality rejects the request, no further action on the matter shall
18 be taken for a period of one year after the date that the governing body rejects the request. After
19 such period of time, the persons residing in the area may submit a new petition pursuant to this
20 subsection. If the governing body of the municipality approves the request, the county clerk
21 shall proceed as prescribed in subsections 2 and 3 of this section.
22 2. Upon approval of the issue by the governing body of the municipality as prescribed in
23 subsection 1 of this section, the county clerk shall present the petition to the county commission
24 who shall thereupon set the petition for hearing not less than thirty days nor more than forty days
25 after the filing.
26 3. Notice shall be given by the county commission of the time and place where the
27 hearing will be held, by publication on three separate days in one or more newspapers having a
28 general circulation within the territory proposed to be incorporated as part of the park system, the
29 first of which publications shall be not less that twenty days prior to the date set for the hearing
30 and if there is no such newspaper, then notice shall be posted in ten of the most public places in
Action Taken___________________________________________ Date __________________
Page 1 of 87
4419H05.03H
1 the territory, not less than twenty days prior to the date set for the hearing. This notice shall
2 include a description of the territory as set out in the petition, the question of incorporation for
3 park system services and the rate of tax which residents within the area outside the municipality
4 would be required to pay to support the park system as set out in the petition.
5 4. If the county commission finds that the petition and notice meet the requirements of
6 subsections 1, 2 and 3 of this section, and that the boundaries as defined are reasonable
7 boundaries for the incorporation of the area into the park system, the county commission shall
8 order the submission of the question.
9 5. The question shall be submitted to the voters within the area outside the municipality
10 [substantially in the following form:] as provided in section 115.706.
[Shall the area be part of the public park system of the ______ (city,
town, village) and shall a ______ cent tax on each one hundred dollars
of assessed valuation within the area be levied for public parks?]

11 6. If a majority of the votes cast on the proposal by the qualified voters within the area
12 outside the municipality voting thereon are in favor of the proposal, then the area shall be part of
13 the municipal park system as of the first day of the year following the year of the election.
14 7. The results of the election shall be certified by the election official of the county not
15 less than thirty days after the election. In the event the proposal fails to receive a majority of the
16 votes within the area outside the municipality in favor of the proposal, then such proposal shall
17 not be resubmitted at any election held within one year of the date of the election the proposal
18 was rejected.
19 8. If the area outside the municipality votes to join the municipal park system, then such
20 an area shall have proportional representation on the park board in accordance with its
21 population to the population of the municipality, except that such area shall be entitled to at least
22 one representative on the park board. The county clerk shall determine the number of additional
23 representatives by dividing the population of the municipality based on the last decennial census
24 by nine to produce the quotient and shall allocate to the area that has voted to join the district one
25 representative per quotient or part thereof which representative or representatives shall be in
26 addition to the nine representatives from the municipality. The county commission shall appoint
27 board members who shall have resided in the area outside the municipality which is included
28 within the municipal park system for terms of three years. Where the area is in more than one
29 county, the county commissions of each county shall, as nearly as practicable, evenly appoint
30 such members with the county commission of the county having the largest area within the
31 system appointing a greater number of board members if the members cannot be appointed
32 evenly. Residents of such area residing outside the municipal boundaries shall have the same
33 right of access to parks and park facilities in the municipal park system as residents of the

4 provisions of this section.

4 "67.990. 1. The governing body of any county or city not within a county may, upon
5 approval of a majority of the qualified voters of such county or city voting thereon, levy and
6 collect a tax not to exceed five cents per one hundred dollars of assessed valuation, or in any
7 county of the first classification with more than eighty-five thousand nine hundred but less than
8 eighty-six thousand inhabitants, the governing body may, upon approval of a majority of the
9 qualified voters of the county voting thereon, levy and collect a tax not to exceed ten cents per
10 one hundred dollars of assessed valuation upon all taxable property within the county or city or
11 for the purpose of providing services to persons sixty years of age or older. The tax so levied
12 shall be collected along with other county or city taxes, in the manner provided by law. All
13 funds collected for this purpose shall be deposited in a special fund for the provision of services
14 for persons sixty years of age or older, and shall be used for no other purpose except those
15 purposes authorized in sections 67.990 to 67.995. Deposits in the fund shall be expended only
16 upon approval of the board of directors established in section 67.993, if in a county, and only in
17 accordance with the fund budget approved by the county governing body.

5 "71.802. 1. Any district established under the provisions of sections 71.790 to 71.808
6 may, upon approval of the constitutionally required percentage of the voters of the district voting
7 thereon, incur indebtedness and issue bonds or notes for the payment thereof. Notice of the
Page 9 of 87
4419H05.03H
1 election, the amount and the purpose of the loan shall be given.
2 2. The question shall be submitted [in substantially the following form:] as provided in
3 section 115.706.
4 [Shall the special business district incur indebtedness for the purpose of ______ in the
5 amount of ______ dollars, evidenced by the issuance of bonds or notes and levy a real estate tax
6 to pay therefor?]
7 3. If the constitutionally required percentage of the votes cast are for the indebtedness,
8 the district shall, subject to the restrictions of section 71.796 and section 71.800, be vested with
9 the power to incur indebtedness in the name of the district, to the amount and for the purposes
10 specified on the ballot, and issue the bonds of the district for the payment thereof.
11 4. The indebtedness authorized by this section shall not be contracted for a period longer
12 than twenty years, and the entire amount of the indebtedness shall at no time exceed, including
13 the existing indebtedness of the district, in the aggregate ten percent of the value of taxable
14 tangible property therein, as shown by the last completed assessment for state and county
15 purposes.
16 5. It shall be the duty of the district to provide for the collection of an annual tax
17 sufficient to pay the interest on the indebtedness as it falls due, and also to constitute a sinking
18 fund for the payment of the principal thereof within the time the principal becomes due.
19 80.460. 1. The chairman of the board of trustees of all towns and villages in this state
20 shall procure from the clerk of the county commission in which such town is located, and it shall
21 be the duty of said clerk to deliver to the chairman of the board of trustees within twenty days
22 after the date of the final adjournment of the board of equalization a certified abstract from his
23 assessment books, as corrected by the board of equalization, on all property within such town
24 subject to its taxing power and the assessed value thereof as corrected by the board of
25 equalization, which abstract shall be immediately transmitted to the board of trustees, and it shall
26 be the duty of such board of trustees to establish by ordinance the annual rates of tax levy for the
27 year for municipal purposes upon all subjects and objects of taxation within such town, which
28 tax shall not exceed the maximum rate for general municipal purposes of fifty cents on the one
29 hundred dollars assessed valuation; provided, however, that the rate of taxation for general
30 municipal purposes herein limited may be increased for such purposes for a period not to exceed
31 four years at any one time when such rate and purpose of increase are submitted to a vote of the
32 voters within such towns and two-thirds of the voters voting thereon shall vote therefor, but such
33 increase so voted shall be limited to a maximum rate of taxation not to exceed thirty cents on the
34 one hundred dollars assessed valuation. The board of trustees of any such towns may submit a
35 question for increase of levy when in the opinion of such board of trustees the necessity therefor
36 arises, and such question shall be submitted by such board of trustees when petitioned therefor
37 by voters equaling in number five percent or more of the voters of such towns or villages voting
38 for mayor or member of board of trustees at the last election at which a mayor or member of

27 92.010. 1. Any constitutional charter cities in this state which may now have or
28 hereafter acquire seven hundred thousand or more inhabitants may levy upon all subjects and
29 objects of taxation a rate for general municipal purposes not to exceed the annual rate of one
30 dollar on the one hundred dollars assessed valuation; provided, that the city of St. Louis may
31 levy for county purposes, in addition to the municipal rate of taxation above provided, a rate not
32 exceeding the rate which would be allowed for county purposes if said city of St. Louis were a
33 county; provided, however, that the rate of taxation for general municipal purposes herein
34 limited may be increased for not to exceed four years, when the rate and purpose of the increase
35 are submitted to a vote and two-thirds of the voters voting thereon shall vote therefor, but such
36 increase so voted shall be limited to a maximum rate of taxation not to exceed thirty cents on the
37 one hundred dollars assessed valuation. The legislative body of any of said cities may submit
38 the question of an increase of levy when, in the opinion of such legislative body, necessity

12 92.031. 1. Such cities may, in the alternative to imposing the levies for debt service and
13 for capital improvements and operating expenses for hospital, public health, recreation grounds
14 and museum purposes as provided for in section 92.030, elect by ordinance to levy and impose
15 an annual tax for debt service and an annual tax for capital improvements and operating
16 expenses for hospital, public health, recreation grounds and museum purposes such as are
17 referred to in subdivisions (1), (2) and (3) of subsection 2 of section 92.030, which tax levies
18 shall be independent of the other tax levies provided for in section 92.030.
19 2. In the event such cities make such election, the limits on individual and total annual
20 tax levy rate referred to in subdivisions (1), (2) and (3) of subsection 2 of section 92.030 for debt
21 service and for capital improvements and operating expenses for hospital, public health,
22 recreation grounds and museum purposes shall not apply. The tax levy rate for capital
23 improvements and operating expenses for hospital, public health, recreation grounds and
24 museum purposes may be increased from its current rate to a rate not to exceed one dollar per
25 hundred dollars assessed valuation by submission to and approval by a vote of the people as
26 provided in section 115.706.
27 92.035. 1. Any city having a charter form of government and a population of at least
28 three hundred thousand, but less than six hundred and fifty thousand and located wholly or
29 partially within a county of the first class having a charter form of government, in addition to the
30 levy and imposition of taxes authorized by section 92.030, may, except as otherwise provided in
31 this section, by ordinance, levy or impose a tax not to exceed the rate of ten cents on each one
32 hundred dollars of assessed valuation of real and tangible personal property located within the
33 city. The proceeds of the tax representing a rate of at least three cents on each one hundred
34 dollars of assessed valuation to be used for the operation, improvement or construction
35 expansion of museum facilities in existence on August 13, 1978, and the remaining proceeds of
36 the tax to be used exclusively for the construction, operation, improvement, or expansion of
37 additional facilities for such museum and no other. The word "museum" as used in this section,
38 shall not be construed to mean or include an art gallery. General admission to the museum's

4419H05.03H
1 facility in existence prior to August 13, 1978, shall be free and open to the residents of such city.
2 Before the city shall impose any tax under this section at a rate which exceeds two cents on each
3 one hundred dollars of assessed valuation, the governing body of the city shall submit the
4 proposed tax rate increase to the voters of the city for approval or rejection at an election.
5 2. The question shall be submitted [in substantially the following form:] as provided in
6 section 115.706.
7 [Shall there be an increased tax levy of ______ cents on the hundred dollars assessed
8 valuation for museum purposes?]

12 not impose the increase. Nothing in this section shall prohibit a rejected proposal from being
13 resubmitted to a vote of the voters.
14 94.060. 1. All cities of the third class in this state may by ordinance levy and impose

20 of the voters within such cities and two-thirds of the voters voting thereon shall vote therefor, but
21 such increase so voted shall be limited to a maximum rate of taxation not to exceed thirty cents
22 on the one hundred dollars assessed valuation.

25 council when petitioned therefor by voters equaling in number five percent or more of the voters
26 of such cities voting for mayor at the last election at which a mayor was elected.

15 3. The board of education of any school district may provide transportation to and from

18 transportation, if the parents or guardian of the pupil agree in writing to pay the actual cost of

20 for ninety school days, which actual cost is to be determined by the average per-pupil cost of
21 transporting children in the school district during the preceding school year. The full actual cost
22 shall be paid by the parent or guardian of the pupil and shall not be paid out of any state school
23 aid funds or out of any other revenues of the school district. The cost of transportation may be
24 paid in installments, and the board of education shall establish the cost of the transportation and
25 the time or times and method of payment.

8 "184.600. 1. A metropolitan zoo district may be established in any city with a

11 district shall consist of such institutions and places for the collection and exhibition of animals
12 and animal life, for the instruction and recreation of the people, for the promotion of zoology and
13 kindred subjects, for the encouragement of zoological study and research and for the increase of
14 public interest in wild animals and in the protection of wild animal life. The boundaries of any
15 such metropolitan zoo district shall be the corporate boundaries of the city, any lands annexed
16 into the city after the establishment of the district and areas adjacent to the city which petition

18 submitted to the qualified voters of the city [at a local or state general, primary or special

16 184.614. 1. Before incurring any indebtedness under the provisions of section 184.612,
17 the board of the district shall provide for the collection of an annual tax on all taxable tangible
18 property therein sufficient to pay the interest and principal of the indebtedness as they fall due

30 percent for cost of collection, which shall be deposited in the state's general revenue fund after
31 payment of premiums for surety bonds as provided in section 32.087, shall be deposited in a
32 special trust fund, which is hereby created, to be known as the "Ambulance District Sales Tax
33 Trust Fund". The moneys in the ambulance district sales tax trust fund shall not be deemed to be
34 state funds and shall not be commingled with any funds of the state. The director of revenue
35 shall keep accurate records of the amount of money in the trust and the amount collected in each
36 district imposing a sales tax pursuant to this section, and the records shall be open to inspection
37 by officers of the county and to the public. Not later than the tenth day of each month, the
38 director of revenue shall distribute all moneys deposited in the trust fund during the preceding
Page 48 of 87
4419H05.03H
1 month to the governing body of the district which levied the tax. Such funds shall be deposited
2 with the board treasurer of each such district.
3 6. The director of revenue may make refunds from the amounts in the trust fund and
4 credit any district for erroneous payments and overpayments made, and may redeem dishonored
5 checks and drafts deposited to the credit of such district. If any district abolishes the tax, the
6 district shall notify the director of revenue of the action at least ninety days prior to the effective
7 date of the repeal and the director of revenue may order retention in the trust fund, for a period of
8 one year, of two percent of the amount collected after receipt of such notice to cover possible
9 refunds or overpayment of the tax and to redeem dishonored checks and drafts deposited to the
10 credit of such accounts. After one year has elapsed after the effective date of abolition of the tax
11 in such district, the director of revenue shall remit the balance in the account to the district and
12 close the account of that district. The director of revenue shall notify each district of each
13 instance of any amount refunded or any check redeemed from receipts due the district.

13 262.598. 1. As used in this section, the following terms shall mean:
14 (1) "Consolidated district", a district formed jointly by two or more councils;
15 (2) "Council", a University of Missouri extension council authorized under section
16 262.563;
17 (3) "District" or "extension district", a political subdivision formed by one or more
18 councils;
19 (4) "Governing body", the group of individuals who govern a district;
20 (5) "Single-council district", a district formed by one council.
21 2. University of Missouri extension councils, except for any council located in a county
22 with a charter form of government and with more than nine hundred fifty thousand inhabitants,
23 are hereby authorized to form extension districts made up of cooperating counties for the
24 purpose of funding extension programming. An extension district may be a single-council
25 district or a consolidated district. A single-council district shall be formed upon a majority vote
26 of the full council. A consolidated district shall be formed upon a majority vote of each
27 participating council.
28 3. In a single-council district, the council shall serve as the district's governing body. In
29 addition to any other powers and duties granted to the council under sections 262.550 to
30 262.620, the council shall also have the powers and duties provided under subsection 5 of this
31 section.
32 4. In a consolidated district, the governing body of the district shall consist of at least
33 three, but no more than five, representatives appointed by each participating council. The term
34 of office shall be two years. Representatives may be reappointed. The governing body shall
35 elect officers, who shall serve as officers for two years, and establish a regular meeting schedule
36 which shall not be less than once every three months.
37 5. The governing body of a district shall have the following powers and duties:
38 (1) Review the activities and annual budgets of each participating council;
Page 70 of 87
4419H05.03H
1 (2) Determine, by September first of each year, the tax rate necessary to generate
2 sufficient revenue to fund the extension programming in the district, which includes annual
3 funding for each participating council for the costs of personnel and the acquisition, supply, and
4 maintenance of each council's property, work, and equipment;
5 (3) Oversee the collection of any tax authorized under this section by ensuring the
6 revenue is deposited into a special fund and monitoring the use of the funds to ensure they are
7 used solely for extension programming in the district;
8 (4) Approve payments from the special fund in which the tax revenue is deposited; and
9 (5) Work cooperatively with each participating council to plan and facilitate the
10 programs, equipment, and activities in the district.
11 6. The governing body of a district may submit a question to the voters of the district to
12 institute a property tax levy in the county or counties that compose the district[. Questions may
13 be submitted to the voters of the district at any general municipal election] as provided in
14 subsection 1 of section 115.706. Any such proposed tax shall not exceed thirty cents per one
15 hundred dollars of assessed valuation. The costs of submitting the question to the voters [at the
16 general municipal election] shall be paid as provided in section 115.063. Such question shall be
17 submitted [in substantially the following form:] as provided in section 115.706.
18 [Shall the Extension District in ______ County (insert name of county) be authorized to
19 levy an annual tax of ______ (insert amount not to exceed thirty) cents per one hundred dollars
20 of assessed valuation for the purpose of funding the University of Missouri Extension District
21 programs, equipment, and services in the district?]
22
23 In a single-council district, if a majority of the voters in the county approve the question, then the
24 district shall impose the tax. If a majority of the voters in a single-council district do not approve
25 the question, then no tax shall be imposed. In a consolidated district, if a majority of voters in
26 each county in the district approve the question, then the district shall impose the tax. If a
27 majority of the voters in a consolidated district do not approve the question, then no tax shall be
28 imposed in any county of the district. In a consolidated district, if a majority of voters in a
29 county do not approve the question, the council in the county that did not approve the question
30 may withdraw from the district. Upon such withdrawal, the district shall be made up of the
31 remaining counties and the tax shall be imposed in those counties. However, if the county that
32 did not approve the question does not withdraw from the district, the tax shall not be imposed.
33 Revenues collected from the imposition of a tax authorized under this section shall be deposited
34 into a special fund dedicated only for use by the local district for programming purposes.

14 10. A county may withdraw from a consolidated district at any time by the filing of a
15 petition with the circuit court having jurisdiction over the district. The petition shall be signed
16 by not fewer than ten percent of those who voted in the most recent presidential election in the
17 county seeking to withdraw that is part of a consolidated district stating that further operation of
18 the district is contrary to the best interest of the inhabitants of the county in which the district is
19 located and that the county seeks to withdraw from the district. The circuit court shall hear
20 evidence on the petition. If the court finds that it is in the best interest of the inhabitants of the
21 county in which the district is located for the county to withdraw from the district, the court shall
22 make an order reciting the same and submit the question to the voters. The costs of submitting
23 the question to the voters at the general municipal election shall be paid as provided in section
24 115.063. The question shall be submitted in substantially the following format:
25 Shall the County of ______ (insert name of county) being part of ______ (insert name of
26 district) Extension District withdraw from the district?
27
28 The question shall be submitted at the next general municipal election date. The election returns
29 shall be certified to the court. If the court finds that two-thirds of the voters voting on the
30 question voted in favor of withdrawing from the district, the court shall issue an order
31 withdrawing the county from the district, which shall contain a proviso that the district shall
32 remain intact for the sole purposes of paying all outstanding and lawful obligations and
33 disposing of the district's property. No additional costs or obligations for the withdrawing
34 county shall be created except as necessary. The withdrawal shall occur on the first day of the
35 following January after the vote. If the court finds that two-thirds of the voters voting on the
36 question shall not have voted favorably on the question to withdraw from the district, the court
37 shall issue an order dismissing the petition and the district shall continue to operate.

17 278.240. 1. The board of soil and water conservation district supervisors of the soil and
18 water conservation district in which the watershed district is formed shall act in an advisory
19 capacity to the watershed district board. When a watershed district lies in more than one soil and
20 water conservation district, the combined boards of soil and water conservation district
21 supervisors shall act in an advisory capacity to the watershed district board.
22 2. Five landowners within the watershed district shall be elected to serve as trustees of
23 the watershed district. The trustees shall be elected by a vote of landowners participating in the
24 referendum for the establishment of the watershed district, but the date of the election shall not
25 fall upon the date of any regular political election held in the county. The ballot submitting the
26 proposition to form the watershed district shall comply with section 115.706 and shall be so
27 worded as to clearly state that a tax, not to exceed forty cents on one hundred dollars valuation of
Page 74 of 87
4419H05.03H
1 all real estate within the watershed district, may be authorized if the watershed district is formed.
2 In watershed districts formed after September 28, 1977, two trustees shall be elected for a term
3 of six years, two shall be elected for a term of four years, and one shall be elected for a term of
4 two years. Their successors shall be elected for terms of six years. In any district in existence
5 on September 28, 1977, the three trustees holding office shall continue as trustees. At the next
6 scheduled election within the watershed district, two additional trustees shall be elected. One of
7 the additional trustees shall be elected for a term of four years and one shall be elected for a term
8 of six years. Each successor shall be elected for a term of six years. In case of the death, loss of
9 landowner standing within the watershed district, or resignation from office of any elected
10 watershed district trustee, his or her successor to the unexpired term shall be appointed by the
11 trustees of that watershed district. A trustee may succeed himself or herself by reelection in this
12 office. The trustees shall elect one of their members as chairman and one of their members as
13 secretary to serve for terms of two years.
14 3. The trustees shall act in all matters pertaining to the watershed district, except those
15 concerning formation, consolidation, expansion or disestablishment of the watershed district. It
16 shall be the responsibility of the secretary of the trustees to see that each soil and water district
17 board included in the watershed district is provided a copy of the minutes of each meeting held
18 by the trustees. The trustees shall be reimbursed for expenses incurred relating to the business of
19 the watershed district.
20 278.280. 1. When a plan of work is approved the trustees of the watershed district,
21 pursuant to section 278.240, shall then by resolution propose that the cost of all works of
22 improvement contemplated in the plan be paid either by a general levy against all real estate in
23 the watershed district, subject to the limitations of section 278.250, or that such cost be paid by
24 special assessment against lands within the watershed district to be benefitted by the installation
25 of the proposed works of improvement, or that such cost be paid by both such general levy and
26 special assessment stating the portion to be paid by each method.
27 2. If the resolution of financing provides that all or any part of the cost of the works of
28 improvement is to be paid by special assessment of benefits the trustees of the watershed district,
29 pursuant to section 278.240, shall appoint three appraisers, who shall be residents of the state of
30 Missouri, and who shall not be landowners in such watershed district, who shall recommend
31 apportionment of the special assessment to the tracts of land which will receive benefits from the
32 installation of the works of improvement proposed in the plan of work. The appraisers shall
33 have access to all available engineering reports and data pertaining to the works contemplated
34 and may request additional legal counsel or engineering data from a registered professional
35 engineer as found necessary to carry out their duties.
36 3. The appraisers shall proceed to view the premises and determine the value of all land
37 or other property within or without the watershed district, to be acquired and used for rights-of-
38 way or other works set out in the plan of work; they shall assess the amount of benefits, and the
Page 75 of 87
4419H05.03H
1 amount of damage if any, that will accrue to each governmental lot, forty-acre tract or other
2 subdivision of land according to ownership, railroad and other rights-of-way, railroad roadways,
3 and other property from carrying out and putting into effect the plan of work heretofore adopted,
4 and shall make written reports of their findings to the trustees of the watershed district. Each
5 appraiser so appointed shall be paid for his or her services and necessary expenses.
6 4. Upon receiving the report from the appraisers, the trustees of the watershed district,
7 pursuant to section 278.240, shall prepare a resolution which shall contain a list of the tracts of
8 land found to be benefitted and the amount of assessment to be levied against each such tract,
9 except that no such assessment against any tract of land shall exceed the estimated benefits to
10 such land by such project. Such tracts of land shall be legally described and the names of the
11 owners thereof shall be set forth beside the description of each tract so listed. After adopting
12 such resolution the trustees of the watershed district, pursuant to section 278.240, shall fix a time
13 and place for hearing any complaint that may be made as to the benefit to any tract of land
14 appraised, notice of which hearing shall be given by the secretary by publication pursuant to
15 section 278.190. The board of trustees at the hearing may alter the benefits to any tract if, in its
16 judgment, the same has been appraised too high or too low. The hearing shall be conducted in
17 the manner set forth in section 278.200. The trustees of the watershed district, pursuant to
18 section 278.240, shall immediately after the hearing pass a resolution fixing the benefit
19 assessment as to each tract of land.
20 5. After the resolution fixing the benefit assessment has been adopted the trustees of the
21 watershed district, pursuant to section 278.240, shall submit the proposal for collection of such
22 assessed benefits to the owners of the lands so assessed for approval and if bonds are to be issued
23 the amount of the issue so proposed, the rate of interest, and the amount of any necessary tax
24 levy in excess of the amount authorized in section 278.250. If two-thirds of the owners of such
25 lands voting favor the proposal as submitted, it shall be adopted. The provisions of sections
26 278.190 to 278.210 and section 115.706 as to notice and procedure and the question submitted
27 shall apply to the referendum held pursuant to this section.
28 6. The trustees of the watershed district, pursuant to section 278.240, shall make the
29 necessary general levy against all real estate in the watershed district and the special assessment

9 emergency services board established in subsection 4 of this section as provided in section

12 service and for expenditures for equipment and services, except for salaries, wages, and benefits,
13 by cities, towns, villages, counties, or fire protection districts which contract with such joint
14 central fire and emergency dispatching service.

1 AMEND House Committee Substitute for House Bill Nos. 2780 & 2668, Page 2, Section A,
2 Line 15, by inserting after all of said section and line the following:

4 "64.401. 1. Persons residing in an area adjacent to and within three miles of a
5 municipality that has formed and established a park system under sections 90.010 to 90.020 and
6 90.500 to 90.570 may petition to become part of the park system in the manner prescribed in this
7 subsection. The petition shall include a description of the territory to be embraced by the park
8 system, the provision for a tax to support the park system at the rate of tax which residents of the
9 municipality are required to pay to support the park system, and the signatures of five percent of
10 the qualified voters within the area outside the municipality as determined by the county clerk on
11 the basis of the number of votes cast in the area for governor in the last election held prior to
12 filing of the petition. The petition shall be filed with the governing body of the municipality and
13 the county clerk. The governing body of the municipality shall within thirty days of receipt of
14 the petition vote to approve or reject the request of the adjacent property owners to become part
15 of the municipal parks system at a regularly scheduled meeting of the governing body of the
16 municipality. The governing body of the municipality shall notify the county clerk of its action.
17 If the governing body of the municipality rejects the request, no further action on the matter shall
18 be taken for a period of one year after the date that the governing body rejects the request. After
19 such period of time, the persons residing in the area may submit a new petition pursuant to this
20 subsection. If the governing body of the municipality approves the request, the county clerk
21 shall proceed as prescribed in subsections 2 and 3 of this section.
22 2. Upon approval of the issue by the governing body of the municipality as prescribed in
23 subsection 1 of this section, the county clerk shall present the petition to the county commission
24 who shall thereupon set the petition for hearing not less than thirty days nor more than forty days
25 after the filing.
26 3. Notice shall be given by the county commission of the time and place where the
27 hearing will be held, by publication on three separate days in one or more newspapers having a
28 general circulation within the territory proposed to be incorporated as part of the park system, the
29 first of which publications shall be not less that twenty days prior to the date set for the hearing
30 and if there is no such newspaper, then notice shall be posted in ten of the most public places in

15 less than thirty days after the election. In the event the proposal fails to receive a majority of the
16 votes within the area outside the municipality in favor of the proposal, then such proposal shall
17 not be resubmitted at any election held within one year of the date of the election the proposal
18 was rejected.
19 8. If the area outside the municipality votes to join the municipal park system, then such
20 an area shall have proportional representation on the park board in accordance with its
21 population to the population of the municipality, except that such area shall be entitled to at least
22 one representative on the park board. The county clerk shall determine the number of additional
23 representatives by dividing the population of the municipality based on the last decennial census
24 by nine to produce the quotient and shall allocate to the area that has voted to join the district one
25 representative per quotient or part thereof which representative or representatives shall be in
26 addition to the nine representatives from the municipality. The county commission shall appoint
27 board members who shall have resided in the area outside the municipality which is included
28 within the municipal park system for terms of three years. Where the area is in more than one
29 county, the county commissions of each county shall, as nearly as practicable, evenly appoint
30 such members with the county commission of the county having the largest area within the
31 system appointing a greater number of board members if the members cannot be appointed
32 evenly. Residents of such area residing outside the municipal boundaries shall have the same
33 right of access to parks and park facilities in the municipal park system as residents of the

4 proposed tax rate increase to the voters of the city for approval or rejection at an election.
5 2. The question shall be submitted [in substantially the following form:] as provided in
6 section 115.706.
7 [Shall there be an increased tax levy of ______ cents on the hundred dollars assessed
8 valuation for museum purposes?]
9 3. If a majority of the votes cast upon the proposal are in favor of the levy increase, the
10 governing body of the city may, by ordinance, impose the additional tax. If a majority of the
11 votes cast upon the proposal are against the levy increase, the governing body of the city shall
12 not impose the increase. Nothing in this section shall prohibit a rejected proposal from being
13 resubmitted to a vote of the voters.
14 94.060. 1. All cities of the third class in this state may by ordinance levy and impose
15 annually for municipal purposes upon all subjects and objects of taxation within such cities a tax
16 which shall not exceed the maximum rate of one dollar on the one hundred dollars assessed
17 valuation; provided, however, that the rate of tax levy of one dollar on the one hundred dollars
18 assessed valuation for municipal purposes may be increased for such purposes for a period not to
19 exceed four years at any one time when such rate and purpose of increase are submitted to a vote
20 of the voters within such cities and two-thirds of the voters voting thereon shall vote therefor, but
21 such increase so voted shall be limited to a maximum rate of taxation not to exceed thirty cents
22 on the one hundred dollars assessed valuation.

24 of such city council the necessity therefor arises, and the question shall be submitted by such city
25 council when petitioned therefor by voters equaling in number five percent or more of the voters
26 of such cities voting for mayor at the last election at which a mayor was elected.

33 the question of continuing such increase of levy at any time for like periods not to exceed four
34 years each.

24 paid in installments, and the board of education shall establish the cost of the transportation and

34 state funds and shall not be commingled with any funds of the state. The director of revenue
35 shall keep accurate records of the amount of money in the trust and the amount collected in each
36 district imposing a sales tax pursuant to this section, and the records shall be open to inspection

Page 48 of 87

4419H05.03H
1 month to the governing body of the district which levied the tax. Such funds shall be deposited

3 6. The director of revenue may make refunds from the amounts in the trust fund and
4 credit any district for erroneous payments and overpayments made, and may redeem dishonored
5 checks and drafts deposited to the credit of such district. If any district abolishes the tax, the
6 district shall notify the director of revenue of the action at least ninety days prior to the effective
7 date of the repeal and the director of revenue may order retention in the trust fund, for a period of
8 one year, of two percent of the amount collected after receipt of such notice to cover possible
9 refunds or overpayment of the tax and to redeem dishonored checks and drafts deposited to the
10 credit of such accounts. After one year has elapsed after the effective date of abolition of the tax
11 in such district, the director of revenue shall remit the balance in the account to the district and
12 close the account of that district. The director of revenue shall notify each district of each
13 instance of any amount refunded or any check redeemed from receipts due the district.

13 262.598. 1. As used in this section, the following terms shall mean:
14 (1) "Consolidated district", a district formed jointly by two or more councils;
15 (2) "Council", a University of Missouri extension council authorized under section
16 262.563;
17 (3) "District" or "extension district", a political subdivision formed by one or more
18 councils;
19 (4) "Governing body", the group of individuals who govern a district;
20 (5) "Single-council district", a district formed by one council.
21 2. University of Missouri extension councils, except for any council located in a county
22 with a charter form of government and with more than nine hundred fifty thousand inhabitants,
23 are hereby authorized to form extension districts made up of cooperating counties for the
24 purpose of funding extension programming. An extension district may be a single-council
25 district or a consolidated district. A single-council district shall be formed upon a majority vote
26 of the full council. A consolidated district shall be formed upon a majority vote of each
27 participating council.
28 3. In a single-council district, the council shall serve as the district's governing body. In
29 addition to any other powers and duties granted to the council under sections 262.550 to
30 262.620, the council shall also have the powers and duties provided under subsection 5 of this
31 section.
32 4. In a consolidated district, the governing body of the district shall consist of at least
33 three, but no more than five, representatives appointed by each participating council. The term
34 of office shall be two years. Representatives may be reappointed. The governing body shall
35 elect officers, who shall serve as officers for two years, and establish a regular meeting schedule
36 which shall not be less than once every three months.
37 5. The governing body of a district shall have the following powers and duties:
38 (1) Review the activities and annual budgets of each participating council;
Page 70 of 87

4419H05.03H
1 (2) Determine, by September first of each year, the tax rate necessary to generate
2 sufficient revenue to fund the extension programming in the district, which includes annual
3 funding for each participating council for the costs of personnel and the acquisition, supply, and
4 maintenance of each council's property, work, and equipment;
5 (3) Oversee the collection of any tax authorized under this section by ensuring the
6 revenue is deposited into a special fund and monitoring the use of the funds to ensure they are
7 used solely for extension programming in the district;
8 (4) Approve payments from the special fund in which the tax revenue is deposited; and
9 (5) Work cooperatively with each participating council to plan and facilitate the
10 programs, equipment, and activities in the district.
11 6. The governing body of a district may submit a question to the voters of the district to
12 institute a property tax levy in the county or counties that compose the district[. Questions may
13 be submitted to the voters of the district at any general municipal election] as provided in
14 subsection 1 of section 115.706. Any such proposed tax shall not exceed thirty cents per one
15 hundred dollars of assessed valuation. The costs of submitting the question to the voters [at the
16 general municipal election] shall be paid as provided in section 115.063. Such question shall be
17 submitted [in substantially the following form:] as provided in section 115.706.
18 [Shall the Extension District in ______ County (insert name of county) be authorized to
19 levy an annual tax of ______ (insert amount not to exceed thirty) cents per one hundred dollars
20 of assessed valuation for the purpose of funding the University of Missouri Extension District
21 programs, equipment, and services in the district?]
22
23 In a single-council district, if a majority of the voters in the county approve the question, then the
24 district shall impose the tax. If a majority of the voters in a single-council district do not approve
25 the question, then no tax shall be imposed. In a consolidated district, if a majority of voters in
26 each county in the district approve the question, then the district shall impose the tax. If a
27 majority of the voters in a consolidated district do not approve the question, then no tax shall be
28 imposed in any county of the district. In a consolidated district, if a majority of voters in a
29 county do not approve the question, the council in the county that did not approve the question
30 may withdraw from the district. Upon such withdrawal, the district shall be made up of the
31 remaining counties and the tax shall be imposed in those counties. However, if the county that
32 did not approve the question does not withdraw from the district, the tax shall not be imposed.
33 Revenues collected from the imposition of a tax authorized under this section shall be deposited
34 into a special fund dedicated only for use by the local district for programming purposes.
35 7. The county commission of any county in which the tax authorized under this section
36 is levied and collected:
37 (1) Shall be exempt from the funding requirements under section 262.597 if revenue

4419H05.03H
1 derived from the tax authorized under this section is in excess of an amount equal to two

8 8. Any county that collects tax revenues authorized under this section shall transfer all

12 9. In any county in which a single-council district is established, and for which a tax has

14 10. A county may withdraw from a consolidated district at any time by the filing of a
15 petition with the circuit court having jurisdiction over the district. The petition shall be signed
16 by not fewer than ten percent of those who voted in the most recent presidential election in the
17 county seeking to withdraw that is part of a consolidated district stating that further operation of
18 the district is contrary to the best interest of the inhabitants of the county in which the district is
19 located and that the county seeks to withdraw from the district. The circuit court shall hear
20 evidence on the petition. If the court finds that it is in the best interest of the inhabitants of the
21 county in which the district is located for the county to withdraw from the district, the court shall
22 make an order reciting the same and submit the question to the voters. The costs of submitting
23 the question to the voters at the general municipal election shall be paid as provided in section
24 115.063. The question shall be submitted in substantially the following format:
25 Shall the County of ______ (insert name of county) being part of ______ (insert name of
26 district) Extension District withdraw from the district?
27
28 The question shall be submitted at the next general municipal election date. The election returns
29 shall be certified to the court. If the court finds that two-thirds of the voters voting on the
30 question voted in favor of withdrawing from the district, the court shall issue an order
31 withdrawing the county from the district, which shall contain a proviso that the district shall
32 remain intact for the sole purposes of paying all outstanding and lawful obligations and
33 disposing of the district's property. No additional costs or obligations for the withdrawing
34 county shall be created except as necessary. The withdrawal shall occur on the first day of the
35 following January after the vote. If the court finds that two-thirds of the voters voting on the
36 question shall not have voted favorably on the question to withdraw from the district, the court
37 shall issue an order dismissing the petition and the district shall continue to operate.

17 278.240. 1. The board of soil and water conservation district supervisors of the soil and
18 water conservation district in which the watershed district is formed shall act in an advisory
19 capacity to the watershed district board. When a watershed district lies in more than one soil and
20 water conservation district, the combined boards of soil and water conservation district
21 supervisors shall act in an advisory capacity to the watershed district board.
22 2. Five landowners within the watershed district shall be elected to serve as trustees of
23 the watershed district. The trustees shall be elected by a vote of landowners participating in the
24 referendum for the establishment of the watershed district, but the date of the election shall not
25 fall upon the date of any regular political election held in the county. The ballot submitting the
26 proposition to form the watershed district shall comply with section 115.706 and shall be so
27 worded as to clearly state that a tax, not to exceed forty cents on one hundred dollars valuation of
Page 74 of 87

4419H05.03H
1 all real estate within the watershed district, may be authorized if the watershed district is formed.
2 In watershed districts formed after September 28, 1977, two trustees shall be elected for a term
3 of six years, two shall be elected for a term of four years, and one shall be elected for a term of
4 two years. Their successors shall be elected for terms of six years. In any district in existence
5 on September 28, 1977, the three trustees holding office shall continue as trustees. At the next
6 scheduled election within the watershed district, two additional trustees shall be elected. One of
7 the additional trustees shall be elected for a term of four years and one shall be elected for a term
8 of six years. Each successor shall be elected for a term of six years. In case of the death, loss of
9 landowner standing within the watershed district, or resignation from office of any elected
10 watershed district trustee, his or her successor to the unexpired term shall be appointed by the
11 trustees of that watershed district. A trustee may succeed himself or herself by reelection in this
12 office. The trustees shall elect one of their members as chairman and one of their members as
13 secretary to serve for terms of two years.
14 3. The trustees shall act in all matters pertaining to the watershed district, except those
15 concerning formation, consolidation, expansion or disestablishment of the watershed district. It
16 shall be the responsibility of the secretary of the trustees to see that each soil and water district
17 board included in the watershed district is provided a copy of the minutes of each meeting held
18 by the trustees. The trustees shall be reimbursed for expenses incurred relating to the business of
19 the watershed district.
20 278.280. 1. When a plan of work is approved the trustees of the watershed district,
21 pursuant to section 278.240, shall then by resolution propose that the cost of all works of
22 improvement contemplated in the plan be paid either by a general levy against all real estate in
23 the watershed district, subject to the limitations of section 278.250, or that such cost be paid by
24 special assessment against lands within the watershed district to be benefitted by the installation
25 of the proposed works of improvement, or that such cost be paid by both such general levy and
26 special assessment stating the portion to be paid by each method.
27 2. If the resolution of financing provides that all or any part of the cost of the works of
28 improvement is to be paid by special assessment of benefits the trustees of the watershed district,
29 pursuant to section 278.240, shall appoint three appraisers, who shall be residents of the state of
30 Missouri, and who shall not be landowners in such watershed district, who shall recommend
31 apportionment of the special assessment to the tracts of land which will receive benefits from the
32 installation of the works of improvement proposed in the plan of work. The appraisers shall
33 have access to all available engineering reports and data pertaining to the works contemplated
34 and may request additional legal counsel or engineering data from a registered professional
35 engineer as found necessary to carry out their duties.
36 3. The appraisers shall proceed to view the premises and determine the value of all land
37 or other property within or without the watershed district, to be acquired and used for rights-of-
38 way or other works set out in the plan of work; they shall assess the amount of benefits, and the
Page 75 of 87

4419H05.03H
1 amount of damage if any, that will accrue to each governmental lot, forty-acre tract or other
2 subdivision of land according to ownership, railroad and other rights-of-way, railroad roadways,
3 and other property from carrying out and putting into effect the plan of work heretofore adopted,
4 and shall make written reports of their findings to the trustees of the watershed district. Each
5 appraiser so appointed shall be paid for his or her services and necessary expenses.
6 4. Upon receiving the report from the appraisers, the trustees of the watershed district,
7 pursuant to section 278.240, shall prepare a resolution which shall contain a list of the tracts of
8 land found to be benefitted and the amount of assessment to be levied against each such tract,
9 except that no such assessment against any tract of land shall exceed the estimated benefits to
10 such land by such project. Such tracts of land shall be legally described and the names of the
11 owners thereof shall be set forth beside the description of each tract so listed. After adopting
12 such resolution the trustees of the watershed district, pursuant to section 278.240, shall fix a time
13 and place for hearing any complaint that may be made as to the benefit to any tract of land
14 appraised, notice of which hearing shall be given by the secretary by publication pursuant to
15 section 278.190. The board of trustees at the hearing may alter the benefits to any tract if, in its
16 judgment, the same has been appraised too high or too low. The hearing shall be conducted in
17 the manner set forth in section 278.200. The trustees of the watershed district, pursuant to
18 section 278.240, shall immediately after the hearing pass a resolution fixing the benefit
19 assessment as to each tract of land.
20 5. After the resolution fixing the benefit assessment has been adopted the trustees of the
21 watershed district, pursuant to section 278.240, shall submit the proposal for collection of such

24 levy in excess of the amount authorized in section 278.250. If two-thirds of the owners of such
25 lands voting favor the proposal as submitted, it shall be adopted. The provisions of sections
26 278.190 to 278.210 and section 115.706 as to notice and procedure and the question submitted
27 shall apply to the referendum held pursuant to this section.

7 of not to exceed three cents per one hundred dollars of assessed valuation may be levied and

9 emergency services board established in subsection 4 of this section as provided in section
10 115.706. All the funds derived from such tax, including any existing surplus funds, shall be used
11 for the purpose of establishing and providing a joint central fire and emergency dispatching
12 service and for expenditures for equipment and services, except for salaries, wages, and benefits,
13 by cities, towns, villages, counties, or fire protection districts which contract with such joint
14 central fire and emergency dispatching service.

20 body has entered into a contract with the center for fire and emergency dispatching services.
